──────── Average over 1000 runs ────────
               total (ms)   retrieval   generation
Long-term   :      7.118       3.397        0.000
ST-cold     :     32.449      32.449        0.000
ST-warm     :      5.651       0.987        0.000

Speed-ups (based on *retrieval* only):
  LT  → ST-cold : 0.10×
  LT  → ST-warm : 3.44×
  ST-cold → warm: 32.87×
────────────────────────────────────────
(enterprise-rag) vonthd@vonthds-mbp:community_implementation$ 


LT → ST-cold : 0.11 ×	ST-cold is slower than querying the long-term DB. 1 ÷ 0.11 ≈ 9 × slower.	The very first hit on the short-term (ST) instance pays the price of promotion: copying entities & paragraphs from the long-term (LT) store, creating relationships, and updating indexes. That one-off cost dwarfs any RAM-disk advantage.
LT → ST-warm : 3.44 ×	ST-warm is 3.44 × faster than LT.	After the promotion is done, answering the next question that stays on the same topic hits nothing but Neo4j’s page-cache in tmpfs. No network hop, no heavy Cypher on the LT store—just a fast index look-up in memory.
ST-cold → warm : 32.87 ×	The second (warm) query is ~30 × faster than the first (cold) one.	That’s the payoff curve of the cache: you invest a single expensive promotion and every subsequent, thematically-related query is two orders of magnitude cheaper.
